         <td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>-10</span> (CKT)</td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th>
         <td><a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">left</a></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Telephone numbers in the Cook Islands">Calling code</a></th>
         <td>+682</td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th>
         <td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:CK" title="ISO 3166-2:CK">CK</a></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th>
         <td><a href="/wiki/.ck" title=".ck">.ck</a></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
          <div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
           <ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em;"> 
            <li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^</a></b></span> As per the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paclii.org/ck/legis/num_act/trma2003130/">Te Reo Maori Act</a>.</li> 
           </ol>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <b>Cook Islands</b> (<a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_M%C4%81ori" title="Cook Islands Māori">Cook Islands Māori</a>: <i>Kūki 'Āirani</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> are a self-governing <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">South Pacific Ocean</a> in <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">free association</a> with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. It comprises 15 islands whose total land area is 240 square kilometres (93&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). The Cook Islands' <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> (EEZ) covers 1,960,027 square kilometres (756,771&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New Zealand is responsible for the Cook Islands' defence and foreign affairs, but these responsibilities are exercised in consultation with the Cook Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In recent times, the Cook Islands have adopted an increasingly independent foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islanders" title="Cook Islanders">Cook Islanders</a> are <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_nationality_law" title="New Zealand nationality law">citizens of New Zealand</a>, but they also have the status of Cook Islands nationals, which is not given to other New Zealand citizens. The Cook Islands have been an active member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Community" title="Pacific Community">Pacific Community</a> since 1980. </p>
      <p>The Cook Islands' main population centres are on the island of <a href="/wiki/Rarotonga" title="Rarotonga">Rarotonga</a> (13,007 in <a href="/wiki/2016_Cook_Islands_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 Cook Islands Census">2016</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> where there is an <a href="/wiki/Rarotonga_International_Airport" title="Rarotonga International Airport">international airport</a>. There is also a larger population of Cook Islanders in New Zealand itself: in the 2013 census, 61,839 people said they were Cook Islanders, or of Cook Islands descent.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With over 168,000 visitors travelling to the islands in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> tourism is the country's main industry, and the leading element of the economy, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Offshore_banking" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore banking">offshore banking</a>, pearls, and marine and fruit exports. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="History of the Cook Islands">History of the Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Western_Pacific_Territories" title="British Western Pacific Territories">British Western Pacific Territories</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Cook Islands were first settled by around AD 1000<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian people">Polynesian people</a> who are thought to have migrated from <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> an island 1,154 kilometres (717&nbsp;mi) to the northeast of the main island of Rarotonga. </p>
      <p>The first European contact with the islands took place in 1595 when the Spanish navigator <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Menda%C3%B1a_de_Neira" title="Álvaro de Mendaña de Neira">Álvaro de Mendaña de Neira</a> sighted the island of <a href="/wiki/Pukapuka" title="Pukapuka">Pukapuka</a>, which he named <i>San Bernardo</i> (Saint Bernard). <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de Queirós">Pedro Fernandes de Queirós</a>, a Portuguese captain at the service of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish monarchy">Spanish Crown</a>, made the first European landing in the islands when he set foot on <a href="/wiki/Rakahanga" title="Rakahanga">Rakahanga</a> in 1606, calling the island <i>Gente Hermosa</i> (Beautiful People).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The British navigator Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> arrived in 1773 and again in 1777<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> giving the island of <a href="/wiki/Manuae_(Cook_Islands)" title="Manuae (Cook Islands)">Manuae</a> the name <i>Hervey Island</i>. The <i>Hervey Islands</i> later came to be applied to the entire southern group. The name "Cook Islands", in honour of Cook, first appeared on a Russian naval chart published by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Johann_von_Krusenstern" title="Adam Johann von Krusenstern">Adam Johann von Krusenstern</a> in the 1820s.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1813 <a href="/wiki/John_Williams_(missionary)" title="John Williams (missionary)">John Williams</a>, a missionary on the <i>Endeavour</i> (not the same ship as Cook's) made the first recorded European sighting of <a href="/wiki/Rarotonga" title="Rarotonga">Rarotonga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The first recorded landing on Rarotonga by Europeans was in 1814 by the <i>Cumberland</i>; trouble broke out between the sailors and the Islanders and many were killed on both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-History_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-19">[19]</a></sup> The islands saw no more Europeans until English missionaries arrived in 1821. Christianity quickly took hold in the culture and many islanders are Christians today. </p>
      <p>The islands were a popular stop in the 19th century for <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> ships from the United States, Britain and Australia. They visited, from at least 1826, to obtain water, food, and firewood.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Their favourite islands were Rarotonga, Aitutaki, Mangaia and Penrhyn. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg/220px-Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg/330px-Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg/440px-Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6020" data-file-height="4312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cook_Islands_Annexation_Ceremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Governor <a href="/wiki/Lord_Ranfurly" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Ranfurly">Lord Ranfurly</a> reading the annexation proclamation to <a href="/wiki/Makea_Takau_Ariki" title="Makea Takau Ariki">Queen Makea</a> on 7 October 1900.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Cook Islands became a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> in 1888, largely because of community fears that France might occupy the islands as it already had Tahiti. On 6 September 1900, the islanders' leaders presented a petition asking that the islands (including <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a> "if possible") should be annexed as British territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> On 8 and 9 October 1900, seven instruments of cession of Rarotonga and other islands were signed by their chiefs and people. A British Proclamation was issued, stating that the cessions were accepted and the islands declared parts of Her Britannic Majesty's dominions.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891-21">[21]</a></sup> However, it did not include <a href="/wiki/Aitutaki" title="Aitutaki">Aitutaki</a>. Even though the inhabitants regarded themselves as British subjects, the Crown's title was unclear until the island was formally annexed by that Proclamation.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1901 the islands were included within the boundaries of the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_New_Zealand" title="Colony of New Zealand">Colony of New Zealand</a> by Order in Council<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> under the Colonial Boundaries Act, 1895 of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The boundary change became effective on 11 June 1901, and the Cook Islands have had a formal relationship with New Zealand since that time.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._891-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When the <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_and_New_Zealand_Citizenship_Act_1948" title="British Nationality and New Zealand Citizenship Act 1948">British Nationality and New Zealand Citizenship Act 1948</a> came into effect on 1 January 1949, Cook Islanders who were <a href="/wiki/British_subject" title="British subject">British subjects</a> automatically gained <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand citizenship">New Zealand citizenship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The islands remained a New Zealand dependent territory until the New Zealand Government decided to grant them self-governing status. On 4 August 1965, a constitution was promulgated. The first Monday in August is celebrated each year as <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Public holidays in the Cook Islands">Constitution Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albert_Henry_(politician)" title="Albert Henry (politician)">Albert Henry</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_Party" title="Cook Islands Party">Cook Islands Party</a> was elected as the first Premier. Henry led the nation until 1978, when he was accused of vote-rigging and resigned. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Davis_(Cook_Islands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Davis (Cook Islands)">Tom Davis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Cook_Islands)" title="Democratic Party (Cook Islands)">Democratic Party</a>. </p>
      <p>In March 2019, it was reported that the Cook Islands had plans to change its name and remove the reference to Captain James Cook in favour of "a title that reflects its 'Polynesian nature'".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraphname_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphname-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-radionzname_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radionzname-30">[30]</a></sup> It was later reported in May 2019 that the proposed name change had been poorly received by the Cook Islands diaspora. As a compromise, it was decided that the English name of the islands would not be altered, but that a new Cook Islands Māori name would be adopted to replace the current name, a transliteration from English.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Discussions over the name continued in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Geography of the Cook Islands">Geography of the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wyspy_Cooka.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Wyspy_Cooka.png/220px-Wyspy_Cooka.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Wyspy_Cooka.png/330px-Wyspy_Cooka.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Wyspy_Cooka.png/440px-Wyspy_Cooka.png 2x" data-file-width="1258" data-file-height="1773"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wyspy_Cooka.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the Cook Islands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Cook Islands are in the South Pacific Ocean, north-east of New Zealand, between <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>. There are 15&nbsp;major islands spread over 2,200,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (850,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of ocean, divided into two distinct groups: the Southern Cook Islands and the Northern Cook Islands of <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">coral atolls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The islands were formed by <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> activity; the northern group is older and consists of six atolls, which are sunken volcanoes topped by coral growth. The climate is <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">moderate</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>. The Cook Islands consist of 15 islands and two reefs. From March to December, the Cook Islands are in the path of tropical cyclones, the most notable of which were the cyclones Martin and Percy.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Two terrestrial ecoregions lie within the islands' territory: <a href="/wiki/Central_Polynesian_tropical_moist_forests" title="Central Polynesian tropical moist forests">Central Polynesian tropical moist forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_tropical_moist_forests" title="Cook Islands tropical moist forests">Cook Islands tropical moist forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_foreign_relations">Politics and foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Politics and foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Politics of the Cook Islands">Politics of the Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Foreign relations of the Cook Islands">Foreign relations of the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_the_Cook_Islands_and_Niue" title="Political status of the Cook Islands and Niue">Political status of the Cook Islands and Niue</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG/220px-Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG/330px-Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG/440px-Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands_-_2006.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The parliament building of the Cook Islands, formerly a hotel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_(7907701948).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_%287907701948%29.jpg/220px-Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_%287907701948%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_%287907701948%29.jpg/330px-Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_%287907701948%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_%287907701948%29.jpg/440px-Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_%287907701948%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_and_Conservation_Event_in_the_Cook_Islands_(7907701948).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Henry_Puna" title="Henry Puna">Henry Puna</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, 31 August 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Cook Islands are a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated state</a> relationship with New Zealand. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government, with the Chief Minister as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Parliament of the Cook Islands">Parliament of the Cook Islands</a>. There is a pluriform<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Monarchy in New Zealand">Queen of New Zealand</a>, who is represented in the Cook Islands by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Monarchy in the Cook Islands">Queen's Representative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The islands are self-governing in "free association" with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. New Zealand retains primary responsibility for external affairs, acting in consultation with the Cook Islands government. Cook Islands nationals are citizens of New Zealand and can receive New Zealand government services, but the reverse is not true; New Zealand citizens are not Cook Islands nationals. Despite this, as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Cook Islands had diplomatic relations in its own name with 43 other countries. The Cook Islands is not a United Nations member state, but, along with <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>, has had their "full treaty-making capacity" recognised by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-art102_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art102-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-map_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map-39">[39]</a></sup> and is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">International Civil Aviation Organization</a> and the UN <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a>, all <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">UN specialised agencies</a>, and is an associate member of the Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific (<a href="/wiki/UNESCAP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCAP">UNESCAP</a>) and a Member of the Assembly of States of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>. </p>
      <p>On 11 June 1980, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> signed <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_%E2%80%93_United_States_Maritime_Boundary_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Cook Islands – United States Maritime Boundary Treaty">a treaty</a> with the Cook Islands specifying the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime border</a> between the Cook Islands and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a> and also relinquishing any American claims to <a href="/wiki/Penrhyn_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Penrhyn Island">Penrhyn Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pukapuka" title="Pukapuka">Pukapuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manihiki" title="Manihiki">Manihiki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rakahanga" title="Rakahanga">Rakahanga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1990 the Cook Islands and France signed <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Delimitation_Agreement_(Cook_Islands_%E2%80%93_France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime Delimitation Agreement (Cook Islands – France)">a treaty</a> that <a href="/wiki/Boundary_delimitation" title="Boundary delimitation">delimited</a> the boundary between the Cook Islands and <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In late August 2012, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> visited the islands. In 2017, the Cook Islands signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Human rights in the Cook Islands">Human rights in the Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="LGBT rights in the Cook Islands">LGBT rights in the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> is illegal in the Cook Islands and is punishable by a maximum term of seven years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_subdivisions">Administrative subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administrative subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>There are island councils on all of the inhabited outer islands (Outer Islands Local Government Act 1987 with amendments up to&nbsp;2004, and Palmerston Island Local Government Act 1993) except <a href="/wiki/Nassau_(Cook_Islands)" title="Nassau (Cook Islands)">Nassau</a>, which is governed by <a href="/wiki/Pukapuka" title="Pukapuka">Pukapuka</a> (<a href="/wiki/Suwarrow" title="Suwarrow">Suwarrow</a>, with only one caretaker living on the island, also governed by Pukapuka, is not counted with the inhabited islands in this context). Each council is headed by a mayor. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg/220px-Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg/330px-Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg/440px-Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="912"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Penrhyn_Aerial_EFS_1280.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Aerial view of Penrhyn
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rarotopo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Rarotopo.png/220px-Rarotopo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Rarotopo.png/330px-Rarotopo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Rarotopo.png/440px-Rarotopo.png 2x" data-file-width="1171" data-file-height="1009"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rarotopo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Districts of Rarotonga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The three <i>Vaka</i> councils of <a href="/wiki/Rarotonga" title="Rarotonga">Rarotonga</a> established in 1997 (<i>Rarotonga Local Government Act 1997</i>), also headed by mayors,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> were abolished in February 2008, despite much controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; border: none;"> 
       <caption>
        The three Vaka councils on <a href="/wiki/Rarotonga" title="Rarotonga">Rarotonga</a> were: 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Te-Au-O-Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Te-Au-O-Tonga (page does not exist)">Te-Au-O-Tonga</a> </td> 
         <td>(equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Avarua" title="Avarua">Avarua</a>, the capital of the Cook Islands) </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Puaikura&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puaikura (page does not exist)">Puaikura</a> </td> 
         <td>Arorangi </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Takitumu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Takitumu (page does not exist)">Takitumu</a> </td> 
         <td>Matavera, Ngatangiia, Takitumu </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>On the lowest level, there are village committees. <a href="/wiki/Nassau_(Cook_Islands)" title="Nassau (Cook Islands)">Nassau</a>, which is governed by <a href="/wiki/Pukapuka" title="Pukapuka">Pukapuka</a>, has an island committee (Nassau Island Committee), which advises the Pukapuka Island Council on matters concerning its own island. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the Cook Islands the Church is separate from the state, and most of the population is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup> The religious distribution is as follows: </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA,_RAROTONGA,_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA%2C_RAROTONGA%2C_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg/220px-CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA%2C_RAROTONGA%2C_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA%2C_RAROTONGA%2C_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg/330px-CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA%2C_RAROTONGA%2C_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA%2C_RAROTONGA%2C_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg/440px-CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA%2C_RAROTONGA%2C_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2612" data-file-height="1560"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CICC_CHURCH_IN_AVARUA,_RAROTONGA,_COOK_ISLANDS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Church in Avarua, Rarotonga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The various <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant groups</a> account for 62.8% of the believers, the most followed denomination being the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_Christian_Church" title="Cook Islands Christian Church">Cook Islands Christian Church</a> with 49.1%. Other Protestant Christian groups include Seventh-day Adventist 7.9%, Assemblies of God 3.7% Apostolic Church 2.1%. The main non-Protestant group is <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> with 17% of the population. <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> makes up 4.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Economy of the Cook Islands">Economy of the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy is strongly affected by geography. It is isolated from foreign markets, and has some inadequate infrastructure; it lacks major natural resources, has limited manufacturing and suffers moderately from natural disasters.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Tourism provides the economic base that makes up approximately 67.5% of GDP. Additionally, the economy is supported by foreign aid, largely from New Zealand. <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> has also contributed foreign aid, which has resulted in, among other projects, the Police Headquarters building. The Cook Islands is expanding its agriculture, mining and fishing sectors, with varying success. </p>
      <p>Since approximately 1989, the Cook Islands have become a location specialising in so-called <a href="/wiki/Asset-protection_trusts#Cook_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Asset-protection trusts">asset protection trusts</a>, by which investors shelter assets from the reach of creditors and legal authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-flyspeck_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyspeck-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> According to <i>The New York Times</i>, the Cooks have "laws devised to protect foreigners' assets from legal claims in their home countries", which were apparently crafted specifically to thwart the long arm of American justice; creditors must travel to the Cook Islands and argue their cases under Cooks law, often at prohibitive expense.<sup id="cite_ref-flyspeck_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyspeck-51">[51]</a></sup> Unlike other foreign jurisdictions such as the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, the Cooks "generally disregard foreign court orders" and do not require that bank accounts, real estate, or other assets protected from scrutiny (it is illegal to disclose names or any information about Cooks trusts) be physically located within the archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-flyspeck_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyspeck-51">[51]</a></sup> Taxes on trusts and trust employees account for some 8% of the Cook Islands economy, behind tourism but ahead of fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-flyspeck_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyspeck-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, the Cook Islands has gained a reputation as a debtor paradise, through the enactment of legislation that permits debtors to shield their property from the claims of creditors.<sup id="cite_ref-flyspeck_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyspeck-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Transport in the Cook Islands">Transport in the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are eleven airports in the Cook Islands, including one with a paved runway, <a href="/wiki/Rarotonga_International_Airport" title="Rarotonga International Airport">Rarotonga International Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> served by four passenger airlines. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Culture of the Cook Islands">Culture of the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
      <p> Newspapers in the Cook Islands are usually published in English with some articles in <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_M%C4%81ori" title="Cook Islands Māori">Cook Islands Māori</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-54">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_News" title="Cook Islands News">Cook Islands News</a> has been published since 1945, although it was owned by the government until 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Former newspapers include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Te_Akatauira&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Te Akatauira (page does not exist)">Te Akatauira</a>, which was published from 1978 to 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg/220px-Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg/330px-Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg/440px-Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rarotonga-8-Maeva-Nui.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Float parade during the annual Maeva Nui celebrations.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The languages of the Cook Islands include <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_M%C4%81ori" title="Cook Islands Māori">Cook Islands Māori</a> (or "Rarotongan"), and <a href="/wiki/Pukapukan_language" title="Pukapukan language">Pukapukan</a>. Dialects of Cook Islands Maori include <a href="/wiki/Penrhyn_language" title="Penrhyn language">Penrhyn</a>; <a href="/wiki/Rakahanga-Manihiki_language" title="Rakahanga-Manihiki language">Rakahanga-Manihiki</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Nga-Pu-Toru" title="Nga-Pu-Toru">Ngaputoru</a> dialect of <a href="/wiki/Atiu" title="Atiu">Atiu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitiaro" title="Mitiaro">Mitiaro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mauke" title="Mauke">Mauke</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Aitutaki" title="Aitutaki">Aitutaki</a> dialect; and the <a href="/wiki/Mangaia" title="Mangaia">Mangaian</a> dialect. Cook Islands Maori and its dialectic variants are closely related to both <a href="/wiki/Tahitian_language" title="Tahitian language">Tahitian</a> and to New Zealand <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">Māori</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pukapukan" class="mw-redirect" title="Pukapukan">Pukapukan</a> is considered closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan language</a>. English and Cook Islands Māori are <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of the Cook Islands; per the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paclii.org/ck/legis/num_act/trma2003130/">Te Reo Maori Act</a>. The legal definition of Cook Islands Māori includes Pukapukan.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Music of the Cook Islands">Music of the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Music in the Cook Islands is varied, with Christian songs being quite popular, but traditional dancing and songs in Polynesian languages remain popular. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Public holidays in the Cook Islands">Public holidays in the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_the_Cook_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Art of the Cook Islands">Art of the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Carving">Carving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Carving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure,_British_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure%2C_British_Museum.jpg/220px-Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure%2C_British_Museum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure%2C_British_Museum.jpg/330px-Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure%2C_British_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure%2C_British_Museum.jpg/440px-Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure%2C_British_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cook_Islands_carved_wood_figure,_British_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>This wooden late eighteenth or early nineteenth century carved <a href="/wiki/Deity_Figure_from_Rarotonga" title="Deity Figure from Rarotonga">figure</a> escaped <a href="/wiki/Emasculation" title="Emasculation">emasculation</a>. Only one other comparable example is known apart from this one in the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Woodcarving" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodcarving">Woodcarving</a> is a common art form in the Cook Islands. The proximity of islands in the southern group helped produce a homogeneous style of carving but that had special developments in each island. Rarotonga is known for its fisherman's gods and staff-gods, <a href="/wiki/Atiu" title="Atiu">Atiu</a> for its wooden seats, <a href="/wiki/Mitiaro" title="Mitiaro">Mitiaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauke" title="Mauke">Mauke</a> and Atiu for mace and slab gods and <a href="/wiki/Mangaia" title="Mangaia">Mangaia</a> for its ceremonial adzes. Most of the original wood carvings were either spirited away by early European collectors or were burned in large numbers by missionaries. Today, carving is no longer the major art form with the same spiritual and cultural emphasis given to it by the Maori in New Zealand. However, there are continual efforts to interest young people in their heritage and some good work is being turned out under the guidance of older carvers. Atiu, in particular, has a strong tradition of crafts both in carving and local fibre arts such as tapa. Mangaia is the source of many fine adzes carved in a distinctive, idiosyncratic style with the so-called double-k design. Mangaia also produces food pounders carved from the heavy calcite found in its extensive limestone caves.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Weaving">Weaving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Weaving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The outer islands produce traditional <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a> of mats, basketware and hats. Particularly fine examples of rito hats are worn by women to church. They are made from the uncurled immature fibre of the coconut palm and are of very high quality. The Polynesian equivalent of Panama hats, they are highly valued and are keenly sought by Polynesian visitors from Tahiti. Often, they are decorated with hatbands made of minuscule pupu shells that are painted and stitched on by hand. Although pupu are found on other islands the collection and use of them in decorative work has become a speciality of Mangaia. The weaving of rito is a speciality of the northern islands, Manihiki, Rakahanga and Penrhyn.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tivaevae">Tivaevae</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tivaevae">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>A major art form in the Cook Islands is <a href="/wiki/Tivaevae" title="Tivaevae">tivaevae</a>. This is, in essence, the art of handmade Island scenery patchwork quilts. Introduced by the wives of missionaries in the 19th century, the craft grew into a communal activity, which is probably one of the main reasons for its popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_art">Contemporary art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Contemporary art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Cook Islands has produced internationally recognised contemporary artists, especially in the main island of Rarotonga. Artists include painter (and photographer) <a href="/wiki/Mahiriki_Tangaroa" title="Mahiriki Tangaroa">Mahiriki Tangaroa</a>, sculptors <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eruera_(Ted)_Nia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eruera (Ted) Nia (page does not exist)">Eruera (Ted) Nia</a> (originally a film maker) and master carver <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tavioni" title="Mike Tavioni">Mike Tavioni</a>, painter (and Polynesian tattoo enthusiast) Upoko'ina Ian George, Aitutakian-born painter Tim Manavaroa Buchanan, Loretta Reynolds, Judith Kunzlé, Joan Rolls Gragg, Kay George (who is also known for her fabric designs), Apii Rongo, Varu Samuel, and multi-media, installation and community-project artist <a href="/wiki/Ani_O%27Neill" title="Ani O'Neill">Ani O'Neill</a>, all of whom currently live on the main island of Rarotonga. Atiuan-based <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrea_Eimke&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Andrea Eimke (page does not exist)">Andrea Eimke</a> is an artist who works in the medium of tapa and other textiles, and also co-authored the book 'Tivaivai – The Social Fabric of the Cook Islands' with British academic <a href="/wiki/Susanne_Kuechler" class="mw-redirect" title="Susanne Kuechler">Susanne Kuechler</a>. Many of these artists have studied at university art schools in New Zealand and continue to enjoy close links with the New Zealand art scene.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New Zealand-based Cook Islander artists include <a href="/wiki/Michel_Tuffery" title="Michel Tuffery">Michel Tuffery</a>, print-maker David Teata, Richard Shortland Cooper, Sylvia Marsters and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Vivieaere" title="Jim Vivieaere">Jim Vivieaere</a>. </p>
      <p>On Rarotonga, the main commercial galleries are Beachcomber Contemporary Art (Taputapuatea, Avarua) run by Ben &amp; Trevon Bergman,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and The Art Studio Gallery (Arorangi) run by Ian and Kay George.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The Cook Islands National Museum also exhibits art.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg/220px-Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg/330px-Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg/440px-Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="525"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tiar%C3%A9_tahiti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Gardenia_taitensis" title="Gardenia taitensis">Tiare māori</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/National_flower" class="mw-redirect" title="National flower">national flower</a> of the Cook Islands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>The national flower of the Cook Islands is the <i><a href="/wiki/Gardenia_taitensis" title="Gardenia taitensis">Tiare māori</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Gardenia_taitensis" title="Gardenia taitensis">Tiale māoli</a></i> (Penrhyn, Nassau, Pukapuka).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>The Cook Islands have a large non-native population of <a href="/wiki/Ship_rat" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship rat">Ship rat</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and <i>Kiore toka</i> (<a href="/wiki/Polynesian_rat" title="Polynesian rat">Polynesian rat</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The rats have dramatically reduced the bird population on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>In April 2007, 27 <a href="/wiki/Kuhl%27s_lorikeet" title="Kuhl's lorikeet">Kuhl's lorikeet</a> were re-introduced to <a href="/wiki/Atiu" title="Atiu">Atiu</a> from <a href="/wiki/Rimatara" title="Rimatara">Rimatara</a>. Fossil and oral traditions indicate that the species was formerly on at least five islands of the southern group. Excessive exploitation for its red feathers is the most likely reason for the species's extinction in the Cook Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>The Islands’ surrounding waters are the home of the <a href="/wiki/Peppermint_angelfish" title="Peppermint angelfish">Peppermint angelfish</a>. While they are common, due to the difficulty of harvesting them they are one of the most expensive marine aquarium fish with a price of 30,000 USD.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cook_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Sport in the Cook Islands">Sport in the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_Oceania#Cook_Islands" title="Cricket in Oceania">Cricket in Oceania §&nbsp;Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Netball_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Netball in the Cook Islands">Netball in the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_the_Cook_Islands" title="Rugby league in the Cook Islands">Rugby league in the Cook Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> is the most popular sport in the Cook Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
